### Supporting Sophie's Request
A rainbow barrier option involves complex correlation modeling across multiple underlyings with path-dependent features (knock-in/knock-out). Here's a quick evaluation of her proposed methods:

1. **3D Finite Difference Method**:
   - High accuracy but computationally expensive (unlikely to meet 50ms constraint).

2. **Longstaff-Schwartz LSM**:
   - Well-suited for American-style options but less effective for path-dependent knock-in/knock-out features due to complexity in backward induction.

3. **Quasi-Monte Carlo with Sobol Sequences**:
   - Ideal for handling high-dimensional correlation while optimizing compute time. Using Sobol sequences improves convergence rate, crucial for a 50ms runtime.

**Solution**:
- Recommend sticking with **quasi-Monte Carlo with Sobol sequences**, as it's the most computationally efficient option for high-dimensional problems like Sophie's.
- Suggest exploring **improved correlation models** beyond Cholesky decomposition, such as principal component analysis (PCA) or copulas, to better capture asset behavior.
